Even that has its reason; it is often better to be in chains than to be free. But I would like to show you how other defendants are treated, perhaps you will succeed in learning something from it. What I will do is I will call Block in, unlock the door and sit down here beside the bedside table.” “Be glad to,” said K., and did as the lawyer suggested; he was always ready to learn something new. But to make sure of himself for any event he added, “but you do realise that you are no longer to be my lawyer, don’t you?” “Yes,” said the lawyer. “But you can still change your mind today if you want to.” He lay back down in the bed, pulled the quilt up to his chin and turned to face the wall. Then he rang.
“我已经等你很久了，”律师在床上说道。他本来正在烛光下看书，现在他把书放在床头柜上，戴上眼镜，透过眼镜锐利地看着K。 K. 没有道歉，而是说：“我很快就会再次离开。”由于他没有道歉，律师没有理睬K.的话，而是回答道：“下次我不会再这么晚了让你进来了。” “我觉得这是可以接受的，”K说。律师疑惑地看着他。 “坐下，”他说。 “如你所愿，”K.说着，拉过一把椅子到床头柜边坐下。 “在我看来，你把门锁上了，”律师说。 “是的，”K说，“这是因为莱妮。”他并没有轻易放过任何人的意思。但律师却问他：“她是不是又纠缠不休了？” “很重要吗？” K问道。“是的，”律师边说边笑，咳嗽了一阵，咳嗽过后，又开始笑了。 “我相信你一定已经注意到她有时是多么的纠缠不休，”他说，拍了拍K.放在床头柜上的手，现在K.又把手收回了。 “那么，”见K. 沉默不语，律师说道，“那更好了。否则我可能需要向你道歉。这是莱妮的一个特点。我早就原谅她了，如果你刚才没有锁门，我现在也不会谈论这件事。不管怎样，也许我至少应该向你解释一下她的这个特殊之处，但是你看我的方式看起来很不安，所以我才会这样做，她的这个特殊之处就在于；莱妮发现大多数被告都很有吸引力。 她依恋他们每一个人，爱他们每一个人，甚至似乎被他们每一个人所爱；然后，当我允许时，她有时会告诉我这些事情，以此来娱乐我。我并不像你看起来那样对这一切感到惊讶。如果你以正确的方式看待他们，被告往往确实很有吸引力。但这是一个值得注意的现象，并且在某种程度上是科学的现象。当然，被起诉不会导致一个人的外表发生任何明显的、可精确定义的变化。但这与其他法律事务不同，他们中的大多数人都保持着平常的生活方式，如果他们有一个好的律师照顾他们，审判就不会妨碍他们。但仍然有一些在这些问题上有经验的人，他们可以观察人群，无论人数有多大，并告诉你其中哪些人面临指控。你会问，他们怎么能做到这一点。我的回答不会让你满意。很简单，那些面临指控的人是最有吸引力的。不可能是他们的罪行使他们有吸引力，因为并非所有人都有罪，至少我作为一名律师必须这么说，也不可能是适当的惩罚使他们有吸引力，因为并非所有人都受到惩罚，因此，针对他们的诉讼只能对他们产生某种影响。不管出于什么原因，这些有吸引力的人中的一些人确实非常有吸引力。但他们个个都很有吸引力，就连布洛克这个可怜的虫子也不例外。”律师说完后，K. 他完全控制住了自己，甚至在最后几句话中还明显地点了点头，以确认自己已经形成的观点。律师像往常一样，试图通过提出笼统的、无关紧要的意见来迷惑他，从而分散他对主要问题的注意力，即他实际上在为 K. 的审判做什么。律师肯定注意到K.比以前更加抗拒，他变得沉默，给K.自己说话的机会，然后，K.也保持沉默，他问道：“你有什么特殊原因吗？”今天来看我吗？” “是的，”K. 说，他举起手稍微遮挡一下蜡烛的光，这样他就能更清楚地看到律师，“我想告诉你，我将立即撤回我对你的代理。”影响。” “我对你的理解正确吗？”律师在床上半直起身，一只手放在枕头上，问道。 “我想你是这样的，”K说，他笔直地坐着，好像在埋伏。 “好吧，我们当然可以讨论你的这个计划，”律师停顿了一下说道。 “这不再是一个计划了，”K说。“也许是这样，”律师说，“但我们仍然不能操之过急。”他用了“我们”这个词，就好像他无意让K.自由，好像即使他不能再代表他，他至少仍然可以继续担任他的顾问。 “没有什么是仓促的，”K. 慢慢地站起来走到椅子后面，“一切都经过深思熟虑，甚至可能太久了。该决定是最终决定。” “那就让我说几句话吧。”律师一边说着，一边把床罩掀到一边，坐到了床边。他赤裸的白发双腿在寒冷中瑟瑟发抖。他问K。 从沙发上递给他一条毯子。 K.把毯子递给他，说道：“你无缘无故地面临着感冒的危险。” “情况已经足够重要了，”律师一边说，一边用床罩盖住他的上半身，然后用毯子盖住他的腿。 “你叔叔是我的朋友，随着时间的推移，我也开始喜欢你了。我非常公开地承认这一点。我没有什么可感到羞耻的。” K. 听到老人以这种感人的方式说话是非常不受欢迎的，因为这迫使他更充分地解释自己，而他宁愿避免这样做，而且他知道这也让他感到困惑，尽管这永远无法使他感到困惑。他改变了他的决定。 “谢谢你对我如此友好，”他说，“我也意识到你对我的案子的参与程度有多深，尽可能深入地为自己服务，并为我带来尽可能多的好处。尽管如此，我最近确信这还不够。考虑到你比我年长得多、经验丰富，我自然不会试图让你相信我的观点。如果我无意中这样做了，那么我恳求您的原谅，但是，正如您刚才所说，情况已经足够重要了，我相信我的审判需要比迄今为止的情况更加积极地进行”。 “我明白了，”律师说，“你变得不耐烦了。” “我并不不耐烦，”K. 有点恼怒地说，他不再那么注意自己的措辞。 “当我第一次和叔叔来到这里时，你可能注意到我并不太关心我的案子，如果不是强迫我想起这件事，可以说，我会完全忘记它。 但我叔叔坚持我应该让你代表我，我这样做是为了帮他一个忙。我本来可以预期这个案子的负担会比以前减轻，因为聘请律师的目的是他应该承担一些责任。但实际发生的情况却恰恰相反。自从您代表我以来，审判对我来说从未如此令人担忧。当我一个人的时候，我从来没有对我的案子做过任何事情，我几乎没有意识到这一点，但是一旦有人代表我，一切就都注定要发生，我总是不停地等着你做事情变得越来越紧张，但你却什么也没做。我确实从你那里得到了一些关于法庭的信息，这些信息可能是我在其他地方无法得到的，但当秘密审判离我越来越近时，这还不够。” K.把椅子推开，站直了身子，双手插在礼服的口袋里。 “诉讼程序进行到一定程度后，”律师平静而平静地说，“没有发生任何重要的新事情。这么多诉讼当事人，在审判的同一阶段，都像你现在一样站在我面前，用同样的方式说话。” “那么，其他诉讼当事人，”K. 说，“都是对的，就像我一样。这并不表明我不是。” “我并不是想证明你错了，”律师说，“但我想补充一点，我期望你能比其他人做出更好的判断，特别是因为我已经让你更深入地了解了该机构的运作方式。法庭和我自己的活动比我平时做的要多。现在我不得不承认，尽管如此，你对我还是太不信任了。你让我过得并不轻松。”律师在K面前是多么羞辱自己啊！ 他没有表现出对自己地位尊严的尊重，而在这一点上，他的地位一定是最敏感的。他为什么这么做？作为一名律师和一个富人，他似乎确实很忙碌，收入的损失和客户的损失本身对他来说都不重要。而且他身体也不好，应该考虑把工作转给别人。尽管如此，他还是紧紧抓住K。为什么呢？是为了他叔叔的个人利益，还是他真的认为K.的案件是一个特殊的案件，并希望能够通过它脱颖而出，无论是为了K.还是永远不能排除这种可能性为了他在法庭上的朋友？尽管K非常厚颜无耻地打量着他，但通过看他是不可能学到任何东西的。几乎可以认为，他是在刻意隐藏自己的想法，等待着看看自己的话会产生什么效果。但他显然认为K.的沉默对自己有利，他继续说道，“你会注意到我办公室的大小，但我没有雇用任何员工来帮助我。过去情况很不一样，曾经有几位年轻律师为我工作，但现在我一个人工作。这部分是因为我做生意的方式发生了变化，因为我现在越来越关注像你自己的案件这样的事情，部分是因为我从这些法律事务中获得了越来越深刻的理解。我发现我永远不能让其他人处理这种工作，除非我想同时伤害客户和我所承担的工作。 但我自己做所有工作的决定有一个明显的结果：我被迫拒绝了几乎所有要求我代表他们的人，只能接受那些我特别感兴趣的人，而且有足够多的生物会扑向我扔的每一个面包屑下来了，而且距离也不是很远。最重要的是，我因过度劳累而生病了。但尽管如此，我并不后悔我的决定，很可能我应该比我拒绝的案件更多，但事实证明，我完全有必要全身心投入到我所接手的案件中，并且成功了。结果表明这是值得的。我曾经读过一篇关于在普通法律事务中代表某人与在此类法律事务中代表某人之间的区别的描述，作者表达得很好。他是这样说的：有些律师带领客户一直到判决通过，但也有一些律师立即将客户扛在肩上，一路扛到判决及之后。就是这样。但当我说我从不后悔所有这些工作时，这是千真万确的。但如果像你的情况一样，他们被如此完全地误解了，那么我就非常后悔了。”所有这些谈话更多的是让 K. 不耐烦，而不是说服他。从律师说话的方式中，K.认为他能听到如果他屈服的话会发生什么，拖延和借口会再次开始，有关文件进展情况的报告，法院官员的情绪如何改善，以及所有他以前听过很多次的巨大困难都会被更充分地再次展现出来，他会试图用从未具体说明的希望来误导K，并用从未明确的威胁来让他受苦。 他不得不制止，所以他说：“如果你继续代表我，你会为我做什么？”律师甚至平静地接受了这个侮辱性的问题，并回答说：“我应该继续我已经为你做的事情。” “我就是这么想的，”K 说，“现在你不需要再说什么了。” “我会再尝试一次，”律师说道，仿佛让 K. 如此恼火的事情也影响了他。 “你看，我的印象是，你不仅误判了我给你提供的法律援助，而且正是这种误判导致你做出这样的行为，虽然你是被告，但你似乎受到了太好的对待。”或者，换个更好的方式来说，处理时被忽视了，明显被忽视了。即便如此，也是有其道理的。被束缚往往比自由更好。但我想向您展示其他被告是如何对待的，也许您会从中学到一些东西。我要做的就是叫布洛克进来，打开门，然后坐在床头柜旁边。” “很乐意这么做，”K. 说道，并按照律师的建议做了。他总是准备好学习新东西。但为了确保自己应对任何事件，他补充道，“但你确实意识到你不再是我的律师，不是吗？” “是的，”律师说。 “但如果你愿意的话，今天你仍然可以改变主意。”他又躺回床上，把被子拉到下巴处，转身面向墙壁。然后他就响了。

Leni appeared almost the moment he had done so. She looked hurriedly at K. and the lawyer to try and find out what had happened; she seemed to be reassured by the sight of K. sitting calmly at the lawyer’s bed. She smiled and nodded to K., K. looked blankly back at her. “Fetch Block,” said the lawyer. But instead of going to fetch him, Leni just went to the door and called out, “Block! To the lawyer!” Then, probably because the lawyer had turned his face to the wall and was paying no attention, she slipped in behind K.’s chair. From then on, she bothered him by leaning forward over the back of the chair or, albeit very tenderly and carefully, she would run her hands through his hair and over his cheeks. K. eventually tried to stop her by taking hold of one hand, and after some resistance Leni let him keep hold of it. Block came as soon as he was called, but he remained standing in the doorway and seemed to be wondering whether he should enter or not. He raised his eyebrows and lowered his head as if listening to find out whether the order to attend the lawyer would be repeated. K. could have encouraged to enter, but he had decided to make a final break not only with the lawyer but with everything in his home, so he kept himself motionless. Leni was also silent. Block noticed that at least no-one was chasing him away, and, on tiptoe, he entered the room, his face was tense, his hands were clenched behind his back. He left the door open in case he needed to go back again. K. did not even glance at him, he looked instead only at the thick quilt under which the lawyer could not be seen as he had squeezed up very close to the wall. Then his voice was heard: “Block here?” he asked. Block had already crept some way into the room but this question seemed to give him first a shove in the breast and then another in the back, he seemed about to fall but remained standing, deeply bowed, and said, “At your service, sir.” “What do you want?” asked the lawyer, “you’ve come at a bad time.” “Wasn’t I summoned?” asked Block, more to himself than the lawyer. He held his hands in front of himself as protection and would have been ready to run away any moment. “You were summoned,” said the lawyer, “but you have still come at a bad time.” Then, after a pause he added, “You always come at a bad time.” When the lawyer started speaking Block had stopped looking at the bed but stared rather into one of the corners, just listening, as if the light from the speaker were brighter than Block could bear to look at. But it was also difficult for him to listen, as the lawyer was speaking into the wall and speaking quickly and quietly. “Would you like me to go away again, sir?” asked Block. “Well you’re here now,” said the lawyer. “Stay!” It was as if the lawyer had not done as Block had wanted but instead threatened him with a stick, as now Block really began to shake. “I went to see,” said the lawyer, “the third judge yesterday, a friend of mine, and slowly brought the conversation round to the subject of you. Do you want to know what he said?” “Oh, yes please,” said Block. The lawyer did not answer immediately, so Block repeated his request and lowered his head as if about to kneel down. But then K. spoke to him: “What do you think you’re doing?” he shouted. Leni had wanted to stop him from calling out and so he took hold of her other hand. It was not love that made him squeeze it and hold on to it so tightly, she sighed frequently and tried to disengage her hands from him. But Block was punished for K.’s outburst, as the lawyer asked him, “Who is your lawyer?” “You are, sir,” said Block. “And who besides me?” the lawyer asked. “No-one besides you, sir,” said Block. “And let there be no-one besides me,” said the lawyer. Block fully understood what that meant, he glowered at K., shaking his head violently. If these actions had been translated into words they would have been coarse insults. K. had been friendly and willing to discuss his own case with someone like this! “I won’t disturb you any more,” said K., leaning back in his chair. “You can kneel down or creep on all fours, whatever you like. I won’t bother with you any more.” But Block still had some sense of pride, at least where K. was concerned, and he went towards him waving his fists, shouting as loudly as he dared while the lawyer was there. “You shouldn’t speak to me like that, that’s not allowed. Why are you insulting me? Especially here in front of the lawyer, where both of us, you and me, we’re only tolerated because of his charity. You not a better person than me, you’ve been accused of something too, you’re facing a charge too. If, in spite of that, you’re still a gentleman then I’m just as much a gentleman as you are, if not even more so. And I want to be spoken to as a gentleman, especially by you. If you think being allowed to sit there and quietly listen while I creep on all fours as you put it makes you something better than me, then there’s an old legal saying you ought to bear in mind: If you’re under suspicion it better to be moving than still, as if you’re still you can be in the pan of the scales without knowing it and be weighed along with your sins.” K. said nothing. He merely looked in amazement at this distracted being, his eyes completely still. He had gone through such changes in just the last few hours! Was it the trial that was throwing him from side to side in this way and stopped him knowing who was friend and who was foe? Could he not see the lawyer was deliberately humiliating him and had no other purpose today than to show off his power to K., and perhaps even thereby subjugate K.? But if Block was incapable of seeing that, or if he so feared the lawyer that no such insight would even be of any use to him, how was it that he was either so sly or so bold as to lie to the lawyer and conceal from him the fact that he had other lawyers working on his behalf? And how did he dare to attack K., who could betray his secret any time he liked? But he dared even more than this, he went to the lawyer’s bed and began there to make complaints about K. “Dr. Huld, sir,” he said, “did you hear the way this man spoke to me? You can count the length of his trial in hours, and he wants to tell me what to do when I’ve been involved in a legal case for five years. He even insults me. He doesn’t know anything, but he insults me, when I, as far as my weak ability allows, when I’ve made a close study of how to behave with the court, what we ought to do and what the court practices are.” “Don’t let anyone bother you,” said the lawyer, “and do what seems to you to be right.” “I will,” said Block, as if speaking to himself to give himself courage, and with a quick glance to the side he kneeled down close beside the bed. “I’m kneeling now Dr. Huld, sir,” he said. But the lawyer remained silent. With one hand, Block carefully stroked the bed cover. In the silence while he did so, Leni, as she freed herself from K.’s hands, said, “You’re hurting me. Let go of me. I’m going over to Block.” She went over to him and sat on the edge of the bed. Block was very pleased at this and with lively, but silent, gestures he immediately urged her to intercede for him with the lawyer. It was clear that he desperately needed to be told something by the lawyer, although perhaps only so that he could make use of the information with his other lawyers. Leni probably knew very well how the lawyer could be brought round, pointed to his hand and pursed her lips as if making a kiss. Block immediately performed the hand-kiss and, at further urging from Leni, repeated it twice more. But the lawyer continued to be silent. Then Leni leant over the lawyer, as she stretched out, the attractive shape of her body could be seen, and, bent over close to his face, she stroked his long white hair. That now forced him to give an answer. “I’m rather wary of telling him,” said the lawyer, and his head could be seen shaking slightly, perhaps so that he would feel the pressure of Leni’s hand better. Block listened closely with his head lowered, as if by listening he were breaking an order. “What makes you so wary about it?” asked Leni. K. had the feeling he was listening to a contrived dialogue that had been repeated many times, that would be repeated many times more, and that for Block alone it would never lose its freshness. “What has his behaviour been like today?” asked the lawyer instead of an answer. Before Leni said anything she looked down at Block and watched him a short while as he raised his hands towards her and rubbed them together imploringly. Finally she gave a serious nod, turned back to the lawyer and said, “He’s been quiet and industrious.” This was an elderly businessman, a man whose beard was long, and he was begging a young girl to speak on his behalf. Even if there was some plan behind what he did, there was nothing that could reinstate him in the eyes of his fellow man. K. could not understand how the lawyer could have thought this performance would win him over. Even if he had done nothing earlier to make him want to leave then this scene would have done so. It was almost humiliating even for the onlooker. So these were the lawyer’s methods, which K. fortunately had not been exposed to for long, to let the client forget about the whole world and leave him with nothing but the hope of reaching the end of his trial by this deluded means. He was no longer a client, he was the lawyer’s dog. If the lawyer had ordered him to crawl under the bed as if it were a kennel and to bark out from under it, then he would have done so with enthusiasm. K. listened to all of this, testing it and thinking it over as if he had been given the task of closely observing everything spoken here, inform a higher office about it and write a report. “And what has he been doing all day?” asked the lawyer. “I kept him locked in the maid’s room all day,” said Leni, “so that he wouldn’t stop me doing my work. That’s where he usually stays. From time to time I looked in through the spyhole to see was he was doing, and each time he was kneeling on the bed and reading the papers you gave him, propped up on the window sill. That made a good impression on me; as the window only opens onto an air shaft and gives hardly any light. It showed how obedient he is that he was even reading in those conditions.” “I’m pleased to hear it,” said the lawyer. “But did he understand what he was reading?” While this conversation was going on, Block continually moved his lips and was clearly formulating the answers he hoped Leni would give. “Well I can’t give you any certain answer to that of course,” said Leni, “but I could see that he was reading thoroughly. He spent all day reading the same page, running his finger along the lines. Whenever I looked in on him he sighed as if this reading was a lot of work for him. I expect the papers you gave him were very hard to understand.” “Yes,” said the lawyer, “they certainly are that. And I really don’t think he understood anything of them. But they should at least give him some inkling of just how hard a struggle it is and how much work it is for me to defend him. And who am I doing all this hard work for? I’m doing it it’s laughable even to say it I’m doing it for Block. He ought to realise what that means, too. Did he study without a pause?” “Almost without a pause,” answered Leni. “Just the once he asked me for a drink of water, so I gave him a glassful through the window. Then at eight o’clock I let him out and gave him something to eat.” Block glanced sideways at K., as if he were being praised and had to impress K. as well. He now seemed more optimistic, he moved more freely and rocked back and forth on his knees. This made his astonishment all the more obvious when he heard the following words from the lawyer: “You speak well of him,” said the lawyer, “but that’s just what makes it difficult for me. You see, the judge did not speak well of him at all, neither about Block nor about his case.” “Didn’t speak well of him?” asked Leni. “How is that possible?” Block looked at her with such tension he seemed to think that although the judge’s words had been spoken so long before she would be able to change them in his favour. “Not at all,” said the lawyer. “In fact he became quite cross when I started to talk about Block to him. ‘Don’t talk to me about Block,’ he said. ‘He is my client,’ said I. ‘You’re letting him abuse you,’ he said. ‘I don’t think his case is lost yet,’ said I. ‘You’re letting him abuse you,’ he repeated. ‘I don’t think so,’ said I. ‘Block works hard in his case and always knows where it stands. He practically lives with me so that he always knows what’s happening. You don’t always find such enthusiasm as that. He’s not very pleasant personally, I grant you, his manners are terrible and he’s dirty, but as far as the trial’s concerned he’s quite immaculate.’ I said immaculate, but I was deliberately exaggerating. Then he said, ‘Block is sly, that’s all. He’s accumulated plenty of experience and knows how to delay proceedings. But there’s more that he doesn’t know than he does. What do you think he’d say if he learned his trial still hasn’t begun, if you told him they haven’t even rung the bell to announce the start of proceedings?’ Alright Block, alright,” said the lawyer, as at these words Block had begun to raise himself on his trembling knees and clearly wanted to plead for some explanation. It was the first time the lawyer had spoken any clear words directly to Block. He looked down with his tired eyes, half blankly and half at Block, who slowly sank back down on his knees under this gaze. “What the judge said has no meaning for you,” said the lawyer. “You needn’t be frightened at every word. If you do it again I won’t tell you anything else at all. It’s impossible to start a sentence without you looking at me as if you were receiving your final judgement. You should be ashamed of yourself here in front of my client! And you’re destroying the trust he has for me. Just what is it you want? You’re still alive, you’re still under my protection. There’s no point in worrying! Somewhere you’ve read that the final judgement can often come without warning, from anyone at any time. And, in the right circumstances, that’s basically true, but it’s also true that I dislike your anxiety and fear and see that you don’t have the trust in me you should have. Now what have I just said? I repeated something said by one of the judges. You know that there are so many various opinions about the procedure that they form into a great big pile and nobody can make any sense of them. This judge, for instance, sees proceedings as starting at a different point from where I do. A difference of opinion, nothing more. At a certain stage in the proceedings tradition has it that a sign is given by ringing a bell. This judge sees that as the point at which proceedings begin. I can’t set out all the opinions opposed to that view here, and you wouldn’t understand it anyway, suffice it to say that there are many reasons to disagree with him.” Embarrassed, Block ran his fingers through the pile of the carpet, his anxiety about what the judge had said had let him forget his inferior status towards the lawyer for a while, he thought only about himself and turned the judges words round to examine them from all sides. “Block,” said Leni, as if reprimanding him, and, taking hold of the collar of his coat, pulled him up slightly higher. “Leave the carpet alone and listen to what the lawyer is saying.”
几乎在他这样做的同时，莱妮就出现了。她急忙看着K和律师，想弄清楚到底发生了什么事。看到 K. 平静地坐在律师床边，她似乎放心了。她微笑着向K.点点头，K.茫然地回头看着她。 “去拿块，”律师说。但莱妮并没有去接他，而是走到门口喊道：“拦住！给律师！”然后，可能是因为律师把脸转向墙壁，没有注意，她溜到K.的椅子后面。从那时起，她就通过在椅背上向前倾身来打扰他，或者，尽管非常温柔和小心，她会用手梳理他的头发和脸颊。 K.最终试图抓住她的一只手来阻止她，在一番抵抗后莱妮让他握住了它。布洛克一被叫到就来了，但他仍然站在门口，似乎在犹豫要不要进去。他扬起眉毛，低下头，仿佛在听是否会重复去见律师的命令。 K.本可以鼓励他进去，但他决定不仅要与律师，还要与家里的一切彻底决裂，所以他一动不动。莱妮也沉默了。布洛克发现至少没有人追赶他，他踮起脚尖走进房间，脸色紧张，双手在背后握紧。他把门开着，以防他需要再回去。 K.甚至没有看他一眼，只是看着厚厚的被子，因为他挤得很靠近墙壁，所以看不到被子里的律师。然后就听见他的声音：“堵在这里？”他问。 布洛克已经悄悄地走进了房间，但这个问题似乎先是推了他的胸口，然后又推了他的后背，他似乎快要摔倒了，但仍然站着，深深地鞠了一躬，说道：“为您服务，先生。” ”。 “你想要什么？”律师问道：“你来得不是时候。” “我不是被召唤了吗？”布洛克问道，这更多的是自言自语，而不是律师。他双手护在身前，随时准备逃跑。 “你被传唤了，”律师说，“但你来得不是时候。”然后，停顿了一下，他补充道：“你总是来得不合时宜。”当律师开始讲话时，布洛克不再看床，而是盯着一个角落，只是听着，就好像扬声器发出的光亮得布洛克无法忍受。但他也很难听清，因为律师对着墙说话，语速又快又轻。 “先生，您想让我再次离开吗？”布洛克问道。 “好吧，你现在在这里，”律师说。 “停留！”就好像律师没有按照布洛克的意愿去做，而是用棍子威胁他，现在布洛克真的开始动摇了。 “我昨天去见了第三位法官，”律师说，“他是我的一个朋友，慢慢地把话题转到了你的话题上。你想知道他说了什么吗？” “哦，好的，拜托，”布洛克说。律师没有立即回答，布洛克又重复了一遍他的要求，并低下头，仿佛要跪下。但随后 K. 对他说道：“你认为你在做什么？”他喊道。莱妮本来想阻止他叫出声，所以他握住了她的另一只手。 让他紧紧握着的不是爱情，她频频叹息，试图将手从他身上松开。但布洛克因 K. 的爆发而受到惩罚，律师问他：“你的律师是谁？” “是的，先生，”布洛克说。 “除了我之外还有谁呢？”律师问道。 “除了你之外没有人，先生，”布洛克说。 “除了我之外，不要有任何人，”律师说。布洛克完全明白这意味着什么，他怒视着K.，猛烈地摇头。如果这些行为转化为言语，那将是粗俗的侮辱。 K. 一直很友好并且愿意与这样的人讨论他自己的案子！ “我不会再打扰你了，”K.靠在椅子上说道。 “你可以跪下，也可以趴着，随你喜欢。我不会再打扰你了。”但布洛克仍然有一些自豪感，至少对K来说是这样，他挥舞着拳头朝K.走去，当律师在场时，他尽可能大声地喊叫。 “你不应该这样对我说话，这是不允许的。你为什么侮辱我？尤其是在律师面前，我们，你和我，只是因为他的慈善而被容忍。你并不比我更好，你也被指控过一些事情，你也面临着指控。尽管如此，如果你仍然是一位绅士，那么我就和你一样是一位绅士，甚至更加绅士。我希望别人能以绅士的身份与我交谈，尤其是你。 如果你认为被允许坐在那里静静地听我趴着听你说的，这会让你比我更好，那么你应该牢记一句古老的法律谚语：如果你受到怀疑，最好移动而不是静止，就好像你静止不动一样，你可以在不知不觉中处于秤盘上，并与你的罪孽一起被称重。” K.什么也没说。他只是惊讶地看着这个心烦意乱的人，他的眼睛完全静止了。短短几个小时，他就发生了如此大的变化！难道是这场试炼让他左右摇摆，让他无法分清谁是朋友，谁是敌人？难道他看不出律师今天故意羞辱他，除了向K.炫耀他的权力，甚至可能借此征服K.之外没有其他目的吗？但是，如果布洛克看不到这一点，或者如果他非常害怕律师，以至于这种洞察力对他没有任何用处，那么他怎么会如此狡猾或如此大胆地向律师撒谎并向律师隐瞒呢？他有其他律师代表他工作吗？而他又怎么敢攻击随时泄露他秘密的K？但他比这更大胆，他走到律师的床前，开始抱怨K。赫尔德，先生，”他说，“你听到这个人对我说话的语气了吗？他的审判时间可以用小时来计算，他想告诉我当我已经卷入一个法律案件五年后该怎么办。他甚至侮辱我。他什么都不知道，但是当我以我薄弱的能力允许的范围内，当我仔细研究如何与法庭相处，我们应该做什么以及法庭的做法是什么时，他却侮辱我。” “不要让任何人打扰你，”律师说，“做你认为正确的事情。” “我会的。”布洛克说道，仿佛是在自言自语，给自己鼓起勇气，他快速地看了一眼旁边，在床边跪了下来。 “我现在跪下，赫尔德博士，先生，”他说。但律师却保持沉默。布洛克用一只手小心翼翼地抚摸着床罩。当他这样做时，莱妮在一片寂静中从K.的手中挣脱出来，说道：“你弄痛了我。让我走。我要去布洛克那里。”她走到他身边，坐在床边。布洛克对此非常高兴，他立即用活泼但沉默的手势催促她向律师求情。显然，他迫切需要律师告诉他一些事情，尽管也许只是为了让他能够与其他律师一起利用这些信息。莱妮大概很清楚如何才能把律师带过来，她指着他的手，抿起嘴唇，就像在吻一样。布洛克立即进行了亲吻，并在莱妮的进一步敦促下又重复了两次。但律师继续保持沉默。然后莱妮靠在律师身上，当她伸展身体时，可以看到她迷人的身体形状，弯下腰靠近他的脸，抚摸着他长长的白发。现在这迫使他必须给出答案。 “我不太愿意告诉他，”律师说道，可以看到他的头在轻微地摇晃，也许是为了更好地感受到莱妮手上的压力。布洛克低着头仔细听着，仿佛听着就违反了命令。 “是什么让你对此如此警惕？”莱妮问。 K. 他有一种感觉，他正在听一段做作的对话，它已经被重复了很多次，而且还会被重复很多次，而对于布洛克来说，它永远不会失去新鲜感。 “他今天的行为怎么样？”询问律师而不是回答。莱妮说话之前，她低头看着布洛克，看了他一会儿，他向她举起双手，恳求地揉搓着双手。最后她郑重地点了点头，转身对律师说：“他很安静，也很勤奋。”这是一位年长的商人，胡子很长，正在恳求一位年轻的女孩为他说话。即使他的所作所为背后有什么计划，也没有什么可以让他在同胞眼中恢复原样。 K. 无法理解律师怎么会认为这样的表现会赢得他的支持。即使他之前没有做什么让他想离开的事情，那么这一幕也会让他想离开。即使对于旁观者来说，这也几乎是一种耻辱。这就是律师的方法，幸运的是K.接触的时间不长，目的是让委托人忘记整个世界，只给他留下希望，通过这种欺骗手段完成审判。他不再是客户，他是律师的狗。如果律师命令他像狗窝一样爬到床底下并从下面吠叫，那么他会热情地这样做。 K.听着这一切，测试它，思考它，就好像他被赋予了仔细观察这里所说的一切，向上级报告并写报告的任务一样。 “他一整天都在做什么？”律师问道。 “我把他锁在女仆房里一整天，”莱妮说，“这样他就不会阻止我干活了。 那是他通常呆的地方。我时不时地从窥视孔里看他在做什么，每次他都跪在床上，靠在窗台上阅读你给他的文件。这给我留下了很好的印象；因为窗户只通向通风井，几乎不透光。他在那种情况下还在读书，这表明他是多么听话。” “我很高兴听到这个消息，”律师说。 “但是他明白他在读什么吗？”在谈话进行的过程中，布洛克不断地动着嘴唇，清晰地阐述着他希望莱妮给出的答案。 “当然，我不能给你任何确定的答案，”莱妮说，“但我看得出来他读得很仔细。他花了一整天时间阅读同一页，用手指沿着线条滑动。每当我看着他时，他都会叹息，好像阅读对他来说是一项繁重的工作。我估计你给他的论文很难理解。” “是的，”律师说，“他们确实是这样。我真的不认为他理解其中的任何内容。但他们至少应该让他知道这是一场多么艰难的斗争，以及我要为他辩护需要付出多少努力。我做这些辛苦的工作是为了谁？我正在做这件事，即使说我是为了布洛克做这件事也是可笑的。他也应该明白这意味着什么。他学习没有停顿吗？” “几乎没有停顿，”莱妮回答。 “有一次他向我要水喝，我就隔着窗户给他倒了一杯水。然后八点钟我就让他出去了，并给了他一些吃的。”布洛克斜眼看了K.一眼，仿佛他受到了表扬，也必须给K.留下深刻的印象。他现在看起来更加乐观，行动更加自如，膝盖来回摇晃。 当他听到律师的下面这句话时，他的惊讶更加明显：“你说他很好，”律师说，“但这就是让我难受的地方。你看，法官根本没有说他好话，无论是关于布洛克还是他的案子。” “没说他好话吗？”莱妮问。 “这怎么可能？”布洛克紧张地看着她，他似乎认为，尽管法官的话已经说了很久了，但她能够改变这些话，对他有利。 “一点也不，”律师说。 “事实上，当我开始和他谈论布洛克时，他变得非常生气。 “别跟我谈论布洛克，”他说。 “他是我的客户，”我说。“你让他虐待你，”他说。 “我认为他的案子还没有败诉，”我说。“你让他虐待你，”他重复道。 “我不这么认为，”我说，“布洛克在他的案子上很努力，而且总是知道事情的立场。”他几乎和我住在一起，所以他总是知道发生了什么。你并不总是能找到这样的热情。我承认，他个人不太令人愉快，他的举止很糟糕，而且很肮脏，但就审判而言，他非常完美。”我说完美，但我故意夸张。然后他说，‘布洛克很狡猾，仅此而已。他积累了丰富的经验，知道如何拖延诉讼程序。但他不知道的事情比他知道的还要多。如果他得知审判还没有开始，如果你告诉他他们甚至没有按铃宣布诉讼开始，你认为他会怎么说？’好吧，布洛克，好吧，”律师说道。听到这句话，布洛克开始用颤抖的膝盖站起来，显然想要请求一些解释。 这是律师第一次直接向布洛克说出明确的话语。他用疲倦的眼睛低下头，一半茫然，一半看着布洛克，布洛克在这种目光下慢慢跪倒在地。 “法官的话对你来说没有任何意义，”律师说。 “你不必对每一个字都感到害怕。如果你再这样做，我不会告诉你任何其他事情。如果你不看着我，就不可能开始一个句子，就好像你正在接受你的最终判断一样。你应该为自己在我的客户面前感到羞耻！你正在摧毁他对我的信任。你到底想要什么？你还活着，还在我的保护之下。担心是没有意义的！您在某处读到，最终的判决往往会在没有任何警告的情况下随时由任何人做出。而且，在适当的情况下，这基本上是正确的，但我不喜欢你的焦虑和恐惧，并且看到你对我没有应有的信任，这也是事实。现在我刚才说什么了？我重复了一位评委说过的话。你知道，关于这个程序有太多不同的意见，它们形成了一大堆，没有人能理解它们。例如，这位法官认为诉讼程序的起点与我的不同。意见不同，仅此而已。传统上，在诉讼程序的某个阶段，通过敲响铃来发出信号。这位法官认为这是诉讼程序开始的时刻。我无法在这里列出所有反对这个观点的观点，而且你也不会理解，只要说不同意他的理由有很多就可以了。” 布洛克尴尬地用手指抚摸着地毯堆，法官所说的话让他一时忘记了自己在律师面前的低人一等，他只想着自己，把法官的话反过来审视。来自四面八方。 “格挡，”莱妮仿佛在斥责他，然后抓住他的衣领，把他拉得稍高一些。 “别管地毯，听听律师是怎么说的。”
